Does not identify image point combinations that allow reconstruction by ray intersection in 3D space. Assistant: Implemented `--debug_stageA` (also accepts `--debug-stageA`) to print **every Stage A hypothesis** (triplet/pair) *as it is tested*, including **frame**, **bodypart**, and the **image coordinates per camera** (plus cam name/index and dlc_id for disambiguation).

This hooks into the Stage A hypothesis loop in `evaluate_hypotheses()` (which is called from `stage_a_for_bodypart()`), so it prints **before any gating/BA** is applied. fileciteturn1file3 fileciteturn1file2

### Patch

```diff
diff --git a/stage_a.py b/stage_a.py
--- a/stage_a.py
+++ b/stage_a.py
@@
 class StageAParams:
@@
     verbose_ceres: bool = False
     trace_ceres_inputs: bool = False
+
+    # Debugging
+    # If True: print every hypothesis (triplet/pair) tested in Stage A, including
+    # bodypart + per-camera image coordinates.
+    debug_stageA: bool = False
@@
 def evaluate_hypotheses(rig: CameraRig, triplets: List[List[Observation]], pairs: List[List[Observation]], params: StageAParams) -> List[Hypothesis]:
@@
     def epi_ok(a: Observation, b: Observation) -> bool:
@@
         d = epipolar_distance_px(rig, a, b, F_cache[key])
         return d <= params.epi_thresh_px
+
+    def _debug_hypothesis(kind: str, obs_list: List[Observation]) -> None:
+        """Print which hypothesis is being tested, with all input observations."""
+        if not params.debug_stageA:
+            return
+        if not obs_list:
+            return
+        bp = str(obs_list[0].bodypart)
+        frame = int(obs_list[0].frame)
+        parts = []
+        for o in obs_list:
+            u, v = float(o.uv[0]), float(o.uv[1])
+            parts.append(
+                f"{o.cam_name}(cam_idx={int(o.cam_idx)},dlc_id={int(o.dlc_id)})"
+                f" uv=({u:.3f},{v:.3f}) lik={float(o.likelihood):.3f}"
+            )
+        print(f"[DEBUG stageA] frame={frame} bodypart={bp} kind={kind} :: " + " | ".join(parts), flush=True)
@@
     # Triplets
     for obs_list in triplets:
+        _debug_hypothesis("triplet", obs_list)
         # Gate 0: epipolar
         if params.use_epipolar_gate:
             if not epi_ok(obs_list[0], obs_list[1]):
                 continue
@@
     # Pairs
     for obs_list in pairs:
+        _debug_hypothesis("pair", obs_list)
         if params.use_epipolar_gate and not epi_ok(obs_list[0], obs_list[1]):
             continue
```

```diff
diff --git a/run_mouse3d.py b/run_mouse3d.py
--- a/run_mouse3d.py
+++ b/run_mouse3d.py
@@
     # Debugging / diagnostics
     p.add_argument("--debug", action="store_true", help="Print per-frame summaries")
     p.add_argument("--debug-save", action="store_true", help="Save per-frame debug JSONL next to output prefix")
+    p.add_argument(
+        "--debug_stageA",
+        "--debug-stageA",
+        action="store_true",
+        dest="debug_stageA",
+        help=(
+            "Print every Stage A hypothesis tested, including bodypart and per-camera image coordinates. "
+            "(Very verbose)"
+        ),
+    )
     p.add_argument("--faulthandler", action="store_true", help="Enable Python faulthandler (useful for segfaults)")
     p.add_argument("--verbose-ceres", action="store_true", help="Let Ceres print iteration progress")
     p.add_argument("--trace-ceres", action="store_true", help="Print inputs to each Ceres solve (very verbose)")
@@
     params.stage_a.verbose_ceres = bool(args.verbose_ceres)
     params.stage_a.trace_ceres_inputs = bool(args.trace_ceres)
+    params.stage_a.debug_stageA = bool(getattr(args, "debug_stageA", False))
```

The new CLI flag is added alongside the other debug options in `run_mouse3d.py`. fileciteturn1file16

### Usage

Add `--debug_stageA`:

```bash
python run_mouse3d.py ... --debug_stageA
```

Example print format (one line per tested hypothesis):

```
[DEBUG stageA] frame=0 bodypart=head kind=triplet :: cam1_top(cam_idx=0,dlc_id=0) uv=(380.729,326.804) lik=0.998 | cam2_front(cam_idx=1,dlc_id=1) uv=(375.551,461.105) lik=0.992 | cam3_side(cam_idx=2,dlc_id=0) uv=(437.833,493.649) lik=0.991
```

No other behavior is changed.

- `TEST :: ...` (observations)

- `INIT ... P_init=(...)`

- `GATE fast_reproj ... -> PASS/FAIL`

- `RESULT ACCEPTED` **or** `RESULT REJECTED reason=...`

Please add another test print to stageA for --debug_stageA that contains the summary telling which configuration is finally accepted for the body parts in the three frames. (I hope you understand what I mean. The hypothesis testing only tells whether a hypothesis is accepted as such. But each body part can only participate in one hypothesis. That needs to be decided. And the result to be documented in the test print.

Background: with option --debug for the investigated frame 0 it says  "3D=0" (see printout). So after stageB no 3D point survives. With the added --debug_stageA prints I want to find whether stage A is the reason for the  final result. Or whether we rather , later , need to search stage B.

Assistant: Done — I added a **final per-bodypart “selection summary”** print that triggers under `--debug_stageA`, so you can see **what Stage A ultimately selects** (0/1/2 hypotheses) *after* all the individual hypothesis tests/gates.

It prints lines with `kind=final`:

- `SELECT ...` summary: how many valid hypotheses existed vs how many were finally chosen
- `CHOSEN#...` for each selected hypothesis (cams/dlc_ids/uv + P + stats)
- `SINGLES ...` listing observations left unused (i.e., not part of the final chosen hypothesis)

It also includes a **diagnostic NOTE** when selection chooses “none” because all hypothesis scores are negative while the “none” option has score 0 (this is very likely related to your `3D=0` symptom).

[Download the updated patch zip](sandbox:/mnt/data/mouse_stageA_final_summary_patch.zip)

This seems to explain the problem. On all three parts selected from the end of processing, though there seem to be accepted reconstruction, it says: NOTE chose_none because best_single=-0.176 < none_score=0.000

Do you see any way to avoid this decision?

Two more questions: Why can the result be SINGLES 6? Does it mean that for both mice there is a body part in each of the images and there is no 3D intersection. And if yes, what happens to the other ones, if it is 4 or 3  only?

To my knowledge there should be an epipolar line gate test. But in the printouts there is none. I only see 4 GATES and an INIT line. Where is the epipolar gate?

Assistant: Yep — that `NOTE chose_none because best_single=-0.176 < none_score=0.000` is the smoking gun.

## 1) Why it chooses “none” even though BA succeeded
Right now Stage A computes a hypothesis score as **`score = -chi2 (+ triplet_bonus)`**, i.e. it’s **always ≤ 0** for any real solution. fileciteturn12file1

Then the selector explicitly includes an option to select **no hypothesis**, and (crucially) the score of selecting none becomes **0** because it sums over an empty set. fileciteturn12file1

So unless a hypothesis score becomes **positive** (which basically never happens with `-chi2`), “none” (0) beats every real hypothesis (negative), and Stage A drops everything.

### How to avoid it
You have two sane options:

**Option A (minimal):** keep `-chi2`, but ensure the “empty selection” does *not* dominate (treat it as `-inf` or only allow it when there are zero valid hypotheses).

**Option B (more correct for “two mice”):** use a **positive, additive** score so selecting two good hypotheses is better than selecting one. A robust choice is “margin to acceptance threshold”, e.g.
`score = accept_rms_px - rms_px (+ triplet bonus)`.
That way good reconstructions have larger positive scores, and two mice can sum to an even larger score.

I implemented **Option B + the safety from Option A** in the patch below.

---

## 2) Why can it be `SINGLES 6`?
Because observations are built as:

- loop over **all cameras**
- loop over **all individuals** (DLC IDs, e.g. mouse0/mouse1)

So with **3 cameras × 2 individuals = 6**, you can get up to 6 observations for a bodypart in a frame. fileciteturn12file3

It does **not** inherently mean “no 3D intersection exists”. It means:

- Stage A ended up not assigning those observations to a selected hypothesis (in your case because it selected *none*), so they remain as “leftover” singles.

If you see **SINGLES 3 or 4**, it typically means some camera/individual entries were missing (NaN coords) or below likelihood threshold, so fewer observations existed in the first place. fileciteturn12file3

---

## 3) Where is the epipolar gate?
It *is* there: in `evaluate_hypotheses`, **“Gate 0: epipolar”**, but it’s guarded by `params.use_epipolar_gate`. fileciteturn12file1

And `StageAParams.use_epipolar_gate` defaults to **False**, so the epipolar test is skipped, hence you don’t see it in your prints. fileciteturn12file1

If you flip it to `True`, then it will run for triplets (all 3 pairs) and pairs (the single pair). fileciteturn12file1

---

## Patch: prevent “choose none” and make scores additive for 2 mice
This patch updates Stage A scoring + selection so accepted reconstructions actually get selected (and selecting two good ones is preferred over selecting none).

Apply by overwriting your `stage_a.py` with the one from the zip (same as your previous patch workflow).

If after this you still end up with `3D=0` after Stage B, then Stage A is no longer the culprit, and we can focus on Stage B’s rejection logic with similar targeted prints.

[DEBUG stageA] frame=0 bodypart=head kind=final :: SINGLES 2 :: cam2_front(cam_idx=1,dlc_id=0) uv=(375.551,461.105) lik=1.000 | cam2_front(cam_idx=1,dlc_id=1) uv=(529.431,466.115) lik=0.979

Chosen are two pair reconstructions (with two singles remaining). That is a good plausibility test. But the first triplet trial goes all the way through the checks to Ceres BA, that is converging after two iterations with rms_px=0.98. I would not complain about that, but accept it. Similarly with another triplet bundle resulting in rms_px=1.519. That one should be the head of the other mouse.

Please advice. Are there reasons for pair instead of triplet acceptance. How can thresholds be changed to arrive at accepting the triplet reconstructions.

Assistant: What you’re seeing is **not** “triplets aren’t accepted” — they *are* accepted (you have `RESULT ACCEPTED` for the triplet hypotheses). The reason you still end up with **pair** reconstructions in the `kind=final :: SELECT ...` step is the **selection scoring**:

### Why pairs win over triplets (even when triplets are good)
In your patched StageA, the per-hypothesis score is effectively:

\[
\text{score} \approx (\text{accept\_rms\_thr} - \text{rms\_px}) + \text{triplet\_bonus}
\]

- Pairs often get **much smaller RMS** than triplets.
- That’s *expected*: with **2 views**, a 3D point can “fit” the two rays extremely well (often unrealistically well), because there’s less constraint.
- With **3 views**, the same point must satisfy **all three** reprojections, so the RMS naturally rises.

So your triplet at `rms_px=0.98` is perfectly fine, but it still loses to a pair at `rms_px=0.055` unless your “prefer triplets” term is strong enough.

### How to force/prefer triplets in the final selection
You don’t change a *gate threshold* here — you change the **selection preference**.

A good rule of thumb from your own numbers:

To make a triplet beat the best pair for the same bodypart, you need:

\[
\text{triplet\_bonus} \gtrsim \text{rms\_triplet} - \text{rms\_best\_pair}
\]

For your head example:
- best pair: `0.055`
- triplet: `0.980`
- difference ≈ `0.925 px`

For the other head triplet:
- `1.519 - 0.055 ≈ 1.464 px`

So **setting `triplet_bonus ≈ 1.5`** is a reasonable starting point for your case.

I prepared a patch that changes **only** the selection preference:
- `StageAParams.triplet_bonus: 0.5 → 1.5`
- and adds comments clarifying it’s a *selection* knob (not an acceptance gate)

**Download:** [mouse_stageA_triplet_preference_patch.zip](sandbox:/mnt/data/mouse_stageA_triplet_preference_patch.zip)

---

## Why there’s no epipolar-gate print
You’re right: you only see ray-angle / closest-approach / bbox / fast-reproj.

That’s because the **epipolar gate exists but is disabled** in StageAParams:

- `use_epipolar_gate = False` (default)
- `epi_thresh_px = 3.0` (threshold only matters if enabled)

So nothing is printed because that gate never runs. If you want it, enable it (and then add a debug print if needed) — but note: your current “ray” gates are already a strong geometric consistency test in 3D.

---

## Practical recommendation
If your goal is “use all cameras when they’re consistent”, the **triplet bonus approach** is the simplest and works well.

If you want something more principled later, the next step would be changing the objective to prefer **explaining more observations** (maximize used 2D detections first, then minimize reprojection error). That removes the inherent “2-view overfits → lower RMS” bias entirely.

User: I finally set the triplet bonus to 3.0 (not feeling absolutely well with it. But better use noisy observations than exclude them for small rms values.)

Assistant: Those per-frame summaries look *healthy* now:

- **`3D` is close to `items` almost everywhere** (e.g. `items=21 3D=20`), which means Stage B is only dropping ~0–2 candidates per frame after Stage A—exactly what you’d expect when things are consistent.
- **`mean_rms_px` ~ 0.8–1.8 px** is a plausible reprojection RMS range for DLC-quality 2D inputs (and comfortably below your Stage A acceptance threshold of 6 px). The fact that it doesn’t explode after your change is the best “sanity check”.
- The dips around frames where `3D=14..16` (e.g. 1783–1787) are also normal: occlusion / confusion / bad 2D points → fewer hypotheses survive.

### About the triplet bonus = 3.0
It’s a blunt instrument, but it’s doing exactly what you intended: **it makes the solver prefer “use more cameras even if noisier”** rather than selecting razor-tight 2-view fits.

The main risk with a large triplet bonus is *not* higher RMS—it’s **wrong 3-view association** (picking the wrong DLC detection in the 3rd camera) being rewarded enough to beat a correct pair. Your current output suggests this is *not happening catastrophically*, because:
- 3D counts stayed high,
- mean RMS stayed stable,
- you’re not seeing sudden stretches of large RMS or lots of dropped points.

If you want a more principled alternative (so you don’t have to “feel uneasy” about 3.0), there are two clean options:

1) **Turn on DLC weighting (`use_dlc_weighting`)**  
   Then the third view can participate without dominating: low-likelihood points get larger σ → contribute less to BA and to chi²-like scoring. This matches your philosophy (“use it, but don’t trust it equally”).

2) **Prefer triplets only when the added view is “not suspicious”**  
   Keep the bonus smaller (or zero), and add a rule like:
   - apply triplet preference only if the *worst* per-camera reprojection error after BA is below some cap (e.g. 2–3 px), or the 3rd view’s likelihood is above some threshold.
   This prevents “bonus-driven” wrong associations.

### What `items` actually means (why it isn’t constant)
In your pipeline print, `items` is the number of **TriangulatedItems returned by Stage B** for that frame; `3D` is how many of those have a valid 3D point (`P is not None`). So `items` can vary because:
- some bodyparts produce **two animals’ hypotheses** (so > number-of-bodyparts),
- some produce **no viable hypothesis** (so < expected),
- Stage B can also keep/reject items depending on exclusivity / model consistency.

So `items=26` doesn’t mean “26 bodyparts”; it means “26 accepted-or-considered per-bodypart-per-animal candidates after B”.

### Next quick confidence checks (low effort, high signal)
If you want to be confident the triplet bonus isn’t silently creating wrong matches:

- Look at **max** RMS, not just mean (a few wrong triplets can hide under a good mean).
- Sample ~20 frames and run with `--debug_stageA`:
  - Verify triplets you’re selecting have the “third view” consistent (small per-camera residuals, not one camera being the outlier).
- Compare `tuneB_dlc_assignments.csv` before/after: wrong-association problems show up as frequent ID flips in one camera.

If you want, paste one `--debug_stageA` “final selection” block for a bodypart where you *suspect* the third camera is being pulled in incorrectly; I can tell you what signature to look for (and what guardrail would stop it without losing your new robustness).

Assistant: ### What’s in `*_triangulated3d.csv`?

One row **per accepted 3D point** (i.e., a StageA hypothesis that survived gating + BA and then survived StageB identity assignment / filtering).

From the code that writes it, the key fields are:

- `frame`, `bodypart`
- `mouse_id` → **the identity after StageB** (your “new_mouse_id” in words). This is the one you should treat as the cleaned/consistent mouse identity (0/1).
- `x_mm, y_mm, z_mm` → the 3D point in mm
- quality: `rms_px`, `max_err_px`, `chi2`, `success`, `term`
- `kind` → `pair` or `triplet` (how many cameras were used)
- `cams`, `dlc_ids` → which cameras and which DLC individual index (per camera) were used for that 3D reconstruction

So: **`mouse_id` in `triangulated3d.csv` is the StageB identity**, not the DLC “individual id”.

---

### What’s in `*_dlc_assignments.csv`?

This is a **2D observation table with identity assignment attached**.

Each row corresponds to a single DLC 2D detection (per frame, per bodypart, per camera, per DLC-individual index) that made it through StageA’s bookkeeping (including leftover “singles”).

Core columns:

- `frame`, `bodypart`
- `cam_idx`, `cam_name`
- `x_px, y_px, likelihood` → **the original DLC 2D observation** (not reprojection)
- `dlc_individual` (what you called `dlc_id`) → the DLC “individual” index from the input file (0/1)
- `new_mouse_id` → **StageB’s decided identity** (0/1)
- `kind` → whether this row came from a `pair`/`triplet` hypothesis (i.e., was part of a triangulation) or is a leftover `single`

So: `dlc_assignments.csv` is **not** “reprojected coordinates”; it’s the original 2D detections plus the pipeline’s chosen identity label (`new_mouse_id`).

---

### Mapping summary (what equals what)

- `dlc_individual` in `dlc_assignments.csv` = **input DLC identity index** (what DLC called the individual for that camera/frame/bodypart).
- `new_mouse_id` in `dlc_assignments.csv` = **StageB identity** (cleaned identity).
- `mouse_id` in `triangulated3d.csv` = **the same StageB identity** (cleaned identity for the 3D point).

So if you want to know “what StageB decided”, use:
- `triangulated3d.csv.mouse_id` for 3D points
- `dlc_assignments.csv.new_mouse_id` for 2D detections (including ones that *didn’t* triangulate)

---

## What does `swap=UNKNOWN` mean?

It **does not** mean “no swaps happened” and it’s **not** computed by simply comparing `dlc_individual` vs `new_mouse_id`.

In StageB, `swap` is a *global state variable* (`SwapState`) that tries to decide whether the **overall mapping** between “DLC individual IDs” and “physical mouse IDs” is confidently:
- `NOSWAP` (DLC individual 0 ≈ mouse 0, 1 ≈ mouse 1),
- `SWAP` (DLC individual 0 ≈ mouse 1, 1 ≈ mouse 0),
- or `UNKNOWN` (not enough evidence / too ambiguous right now).

It can be `UNKNOWN` for very normal reasons, e.g.:

1) **Not enough reliable anchor continuity** (StageB relies on anchor parts like `head`, `tail_root` to score swap vs no-swap over time). If anchors are missing, noisy, or symmetric, it refuses to commit.

2) **The “swap vs no-swap” costs are too close** (StageB uses a threshold `tau_swap`; if `|cost_swap - cost_noswap| < tau_swap`, it stays `UNKNOWN` on purpose to avoid false swap flips).

3) **Large gaps / lost tracking** (if the prior state is stale, it won’t trust it and may drop back to `UNKNOWN`).

Crucially: even with `swap=UNKNOWN`, StageB still assigns `new_mouse_id` to each triangulated item and to leftover singles using segmentation/exclusive votes and the assignment logic. That’s why your outputs can be perfectly usable while `swap` stays `UNKNOWN`.

---

## “Shouldn’t there be swaps when comparing `dlc_id` with `new_mouse_id`?”

Only **if** DLC actually mislabeled identities in those frames *and* StageB corrected them. Many datasets have long stretches where DLC’s “individual 0/1” is already consistent, so you’d see almost no mismatch.

Also, because StageA associates across cameras, you can get cases where a *single 3D point* uses a mixture of DLC individuals across cameras (e.g., `dlc_ids=[0,1,0]`) and StageB still assigns a consistent `mouse_id`. In that case, “swap” is not a single global flip—it’s per-observation/per-camera inconsistency that 3D association resolves.

If you want a concrete “did StageB relabel DLC identities?” metric, compute it from `dlc_assignments.csv`, e.g. fraction of rows where `dlc_individual != new_mouse_id`, optionally restricted to anchor parts or high-likelihood points.

Here’s a minimal snippet you can run:

```python
import pandas as pd

df = pd.read_csv("..._dlc_assignments.csv")

df["mismatch"] = (df["dlc_individual"] != df["new_mouse_id"])
print("overall mismatch rate:", df["mismatch"].mean())

# per frame mismatch rate
per_frame = df.groupby("frame")["mismatch"].mean()
print(per_frame.describe())

# focus on anchors (if those are your anchors)
anchors = df[df["bodypart"].isin(["head", "tail_root"])]
print("anchor mismatch rate:", (anchors["dlc_individual"] != anchors["new_mouse_id"]).mean())
```

If that mismatch rate is low, it doesn’t mean the 3D reasoning is useless—it can still be doing the *more important job* of rejecting wrong cross-view pairings and producing stable 3D points. It just means “identity swap correction” wasn’t frequently needed (or wasn’t confidently detectable as a global swap).

---

## If you *want* `swap` to stop being `UNKNOWN`

The lever is **StageB’s swap decision confidence**, not StageA.

Typical knobs:
- decrease `tau_swap` (more willing to commit to SWAP/NOSWAP instead of UNKNOWN)
- add / change `anchor_parts` (use more distinctive anchors than just head/tail_root, if available)
- reduce `sigma_motion_anchor` (makes costs more sensitive to mismatches; can increase confidence but also risk false swaps)
- increase `carry_swap_max_gap` (keeps state across short failures)

If you tell me which bodyparts are most stable in your setup (often `spine_mid`, `hip`, `snout`, etc. if available), I can recommend a robust anchor set and parameter direction that reduces false swap flips without getting stuck at `UNKNOWN`.

Assistant: Added `--debug_stageB` with **screen-only** logging (no behavior changes) across Stage B.

What it prints per frame:

- **Frame header** + **segmentation source** for each camera (video filename `...mp4#frame=N` or mask png path)
- **Kernel radius/sigma** (the circle used around each DLC 2D point)
- For every **DLC observation used in Stage B**:
  - `frac(bg,m0,m1)` inside the circle
  - the **Stage B vote** it produces (`mouse0/mouse1/none`)
- For every triangulated item: its **vote totals** and **exclusive** status
- **Swap decision diagnostics** (`C_no/C_sw`, per-anchor-part costs)
- **Mouse model summary** (centroids/axes + which anchor parts got assigned)
- When resolving ambiguous assignments: the **assignment_cost** comparisons (`c01 vs c10`, `c0 vs c1`)
- Final per-bodypart summary of what got assigned
